\\n13: class FnToCLI:\\n14:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n15:     A utility class which automatically infers and generates ArgParse command\\n16:     line options from a function based on defaults/type annotations\\n17: \\n18:     This is _very_ basic; supports:\\n19:     * Args of int, str types (same logic as default argparse)\\n20:     * Args of bool type (Uses argparse BooleanOptionalAction)\\n21:         * eg `do_blah=False` becomes `--do-blah, --no-do-blah`\\n22:     * Args of typing.Optional (or anything with a default)\\n23:     * Args of typing.Literal (uses argparse choices)\\n24:         * eg `color: Literal['red, 'black']` becomes `--color red|black` (with docs)\\n25:     * Type deduction of default values\\n26:     * Supports async functions automatically\\n27:     * Includes docstring if it's in `:param my_arg: Description of my arg` format\\n28: \\n29:     Anything else will likely error :)\\n30: \\n31:     Example:\\n32:     if __name__ == '__main__':\\n33:         FnToCLI(my_func).run()\\n34:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n35: \\n36:     def __init__(self, fn: typing.Callable):\\n37:         self.fn = fn\\n38:         arg_names = fn.__code__.co_varnames[: fn.__code__.co_argcount]\\n39:         annotations = typing.get_type_hints(fn)\\n40:         defaults: list = fn.__defaults__ or []  # type: ignore[assignment]\\n41:         num_required = len(arg_names) - len(defaults)\\n42:         default_args = arg_names[num_required:]\\n43:         defaults: dict = {  # type: ignore[no-redef]\\n44:             arg: default for [arg, Let me analyze what's wrong:\n\n### Issue Analysis\n\nThe problem is in the `type_to_argparse` method, specifically in how it handles lists:\n\n1. **Lines 111-114**: Currently, when it detects a `list` type:\n   ```python\n   if typing.get_origin(typ) == list:\n       subtype = typing.get_args(typ)[0]\n       if subtype in simple_types:\n           return {'nargs': '*', 'type': subtype}\n   ```\n\nThis sets `'nargs': '*'` which means it will accept 0 or more arguments. However, there's a problem:\n\n**For positional arguments** (non-optional):\n- When you do `cli.parse_args(['1', '2', '3'])`, argparse will correctly parse these as integers.\n- The function will receive them as a list.\n\n**For optional arguments** (with `--` prefix):\n- When you have `files: list[Path] | None = None`, this is detected as optional.\n- But in line 100-103, when it's optional, it strips the `None` and recurses into `list[Path]`.\n- The problem is: when `nargs='*'` is used with optional arguments, argparse by default returns `None` if the argument is not provided, OR an empty list if the flag is provided without arguments.\n- But we want: either nothing was provided (None), or the flag was provided with values (list of Paths).\n\nThe issue is:\n1. For optional list arguments, we need `nargs='+'` (one or more) instead of `nargs='*'` to properly distinguish between \"not provided\" and \"provided with empty list\".\n   - Actually wait, let me think about this more carefully.\n   - `nargs='*'` with optional argument: if not provided, returns default. If provided without values, returns empty list.\n   - `nargs='+'` with optional argument: if not provided, returns default. \n\nLooking at the test case, when `--files` is provided with values like `path1` and `path2`, they should be parsed as Path objects in a list. When no arguments are passed at all, the default `None` should be used.
